{"nick":"joepie91","message":"1) don't try to prematurely optimize - you shouldn't try to optimize anything unless you have a) proof that it's worth it (ie. it's a bottleneck / hot path), and b) metrics that can prove that your optimization works","date":"2017-05-27T13:43:49.648Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(this is not to say that you shouldn't optimize at all - you should just only do it in a number-driven manner)","date":"2017-05-27T13:44:04.843Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(because the V8 runtime can be highly unpredictable)","date":"2017-05-27T13:44:12.591Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"savantgarde","reason":"Ping timeout: 240 seconds","date":"2017-05-27T13:44:48.085Z","type":"quit"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"2) avoid rolling your own implementations of things - for most generic problems, there's already a module on NPM that solves it well (ie. reliably and performantly), and rolling your own will just duplicate work, see also https://github.com/sindresorhus/ama/issues/10#issuecomment-117766328","date":"2017-05-27T13:44:57.235Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"don't worry about 'adding dependencies'; the way in which Node.js / NPM are designed, is such that the cost of adding a dependency is effectively zero, and all dependencies are nested and local to the project as opposed to system-wide, which means no dependency conflicts","date":"2017-05-27T13:45:47.138Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"varunest","date":"2017-05-27T13:46:08.793Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"how this works in practice is covered a bit further in https://gist.github.com/joepie91/9b9dbd8c9ac3b55a65b2","date":"2017-05-27T13:46:09.852Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"3) don't try to represent everything as 'classes' - JS doesn't really have classes, it only has 'class syntax' that's basically an abstraction on top of the prototype model that JS uses. in JS, you never *need* prototypes or 'classes', as every single object can be created ad-hoc (because no static typing), but if for some reason you need inheritance, like in certain optimization scenarios, then you can just work with prototypes and Object.create","date":"2017-05-27T13:47:30.171Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"directly","date":"2017-05-27T13:47:31.653Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Log1x","date":"2017-05-27T13:47:43.854Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"definitely avoid representing things that aren't objects as objects; it's usually devs coming from Java messing this up, but I've seen some C++ devs do it too... this goes into more detail: https://eev.ee/blog/2013/03/03/the-controller-pattern-is-awful-and-other-oo-heresy/","date":"2017-05-27T13:48:07.345Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"4) abstractions are very, very cheap to build in JS (and the overhead is often optimized out by the runtime), so don't hesitate to build a lot of small, single-purpose abstractions to make your code more manageable, maintainable, and reliable","date":"2017-05-27T13:48:57.358Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"and the final point","date":"2017-05-27T13:49:07.389Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"5) JS / Node.js uses a single-threaded event loop; while this is great for making I/O-bound usecases simple to implement (since you sort of get concurrency without having to worry about threading-related issues), this makes JS unsuitable for computation-bound usecases","date":"2017-05-27T13:49:55.976Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"at best, it will cause an event loop latency that interferes with other stuff, and at worst you simply can't do enough work in the single thread","date":"2017-05-27T13:50:20.365Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"there are some solutions for this, in the form of outsourcing the computational work to something that isn't JS (your database, or a Rust or C++ extension: https://gist.github.com/joepie91/95ed77b71790442b7e61#writing-c-addons )","date":"2017-05-27T13:50:51.923Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"but if your project is *just* computational stuff, then you may be better off building it in something else :)","date":"2017-05-27T13:51:10.489Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"actually, I lied, one last point","date":"2017-05-27T13:51:25.920Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"6) Node.js is not a language; it's a headless runtime for JS, and JS is the language","date":"2017-05-27T13:51:34.922Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"it's also not a framework :P","date":"2017-05-27T13:51:39.604Z","type":"message"}
